## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (ordinary differential equation rate laws)
**Analysis**: The target is dA_dt, the time-derivative of a concentration A(t), which is the standard object modeled by reaction-rate laws in chemical kinetics. With only (t, A) available, plausible structures are reaction-order rate laws, reversible/approach-to-equilibrium kinetics, autocatalytic/logistic-type kinetics, inhibition/saturation effects, and explicit time-varying rate coefficients (e.g., catalyst deactivation).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 (constant-rate consumption/production when reactant is in excess or surface-limited)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive/thermal decomposition analogs)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular consumption with other reactant effectively equal to A or constant folded into c0)
- General n-th order kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical reaction order c1)
- Reversible first-order / relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (approach to equilibrium concentration c1)
- Autocatalytic (quadratic) growth/decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (self-amplification with depletion/limitation; logistic-type chemistry)
- Inhibited first-order (rate suppressed by A): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (c1 + A) (product inhibition or site saturation limiting further consumption)
- Inhibited higher-order: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative/inhibition-like saturation in net rate)
- Time-varying first-order rate (e.g., deactivating catalyst): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) * A (rate coefficient relaxes in time)
- Periodic forcing of rate (e.g., modulated illumination/temperature): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * A (externally driven time-dependent kinetics)
- Power-law time dependence of rate coefficient: dA_dt = -c0 * t**c1 * A (aging/transport-limited effective rate scaling with time)
- Mixed linear + nonlinear consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (parallel first- and second-order pathways)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Straight-line in dA_dt vs A suggests first-order; curvature upward with A suggests higher-than-first order (A**n with n>1).
- If dA_dt is approximately constant over wide A ranges, a zero-order term (-c0) is likely (surface/flux-limited regime).
- If dA_dt changes sign at A ≈ constant and tends to restore A toward that value, include a relaxation term -(A - c1) (reversible/approach-to-equilibrium).
- If dA_dt is small at both low A and high A but peaks at intermediate A, a logistic/autocatalytic form A*(c1-A) is indicated.
- If increasing A eventually stops increasing |dA_dt| (sublinear dependence at high A), use saturation/inhibition rational forms like A/(c1+A) or A**n/(c + A**n).
- If the apparent rate constant inferred from -dA_dt/A decreases over time, incorporate explicit time dependence such as exp(-c*t) multiplying A (catalyst deactivation, fouling).
- If -dA_dt/A oscillates with time, include sinusoidal modulation in the effective rate coefficient (periodic forcing).
- If early-time kinetics differ systematically from late-time kinetics without oscillation, consider rate coefficients scaling as t**c (diffusion/transport-limited effective kinetics).
- If data show a linear term dominating at low A but faster-than-linear consumption at high A, combine parallel pathways (-c0*A - c1*A**2).

GT is the fixed function
\[
F(t,A)=0.2084703204063362\,A^{1/3}\;-\;0.6750544468008356\,A\,e^{-0.0783132263146032\,t}.
\]
So any matching candidate must be able to represent **exactly two terms**: one proportional to \(A^{1/3}\) (with no \(t\)-dependence) and one proportional to \(A e^{kt}\) with \(k=-0.0783132263\), and **no other residual dependence** (no logs, trig, extra powers, constants, rational-in-\(A\) terms, etc.). Also note GT uses \(A^{1/3}\), not \(|A|^{1/3}\); if a candidate uses \(|A|^{1/3}\), it cannot equal \(A^{1/3}\) for all real \(A\) (they differ for \(A<0\)).

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can set its free constants to get exactly \(F(t,A)\) for all \(t,A\).

### 1.
Has log terms and \(|A|^{c8}\) term. Logs cannot be made into a pure power for all \(A\) (unless coefficient 0). If set log coefficients to 0, left with \(c6 e^{c7 t}|A|^{c8}\): cannot produce simultaneously \(A e^{kt}\) and \(A^{1/3}\) (only one term). **No.**

### 2.
\(A c0 e^{c1 t} + A c2\sin(\cdot)+ c5|A|^{1/3}\). Can kill sine by \(c2=0\). Then have \(A c0 e^{c1 t} + c5|A|^{1/3}\). \(|A|^{1/3}\neq A^{1/3}\) for \(A<0\). **No.**

### 3.
\(c0 A^{1/3} + A c1 e^{c2 t} + A c3\sin(\cdot)\). Set \(c3=0\). Then choose

- \(c1=-0.6750544468008356\)
- \(c2=-0.0783132263146032\)
This matches GT exactly. **Yes.**
